<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:1.35em;"><b>Footnotes&#160;/ references</b><br />
<sup id="cite_ref-Form10K_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Form10K-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OurBusiness_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OurBusiness-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AsdaUK_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AsdaUK-7">[7]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Wal-Mart Stores, Inc.</b><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/ɔː/ 'au' in 'fraud'">ɔː</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɑːr/ 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span></span>/</a></span></span>), <a href="/wiki/Doing_business_as" class="mw-redirect" title="Doing business as">doing business as</a> <b>Walmart</b>, is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/Retail" title="Retail">retailing</a> <a href="/wiki/Corporation" title="Corporation">corporation</a> that operates as a chain of <a href="/wiki/Hypermarket" title="Hypermarket">hypermarkets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Discount_department_store" class="mw-redirect" title="Discount department store">discount department stores</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grocery_store" title="Grocery store">grocery stores</a>. Headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Bentonville,_Arkansas" title="Bentonville, Arkansas">Bentonville, Arkansas</a>, the company was founded by <a href="/wiki/Sam_Walton" title="Sam Walton">Sam Walton</a> in 1962 and <a href="/wiki/Incorporation_(business)" title="Incorporation (business)">incorporated</a> on October 31, 1969. As of January 31, 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Walmart has 11,695 stores and clubs in 28<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>countries, under a total of 63<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>banners.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2016_Annual_Report_Page_19_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_Annual_Report_Page_19-9">[9]</a></sup> The company operates under the name Walmart in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. It operates as <a href="/wiki/Walmart_de_M%C3%A9xico_y_Centroam%C3%A9rica" title="Walmart de México y Centroamérica">Walmart de México y Centroamérica</a> in Mexico and Central America, as <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a> in the United Kingdom, as the <a href="/wiki/Seiyu_Group" title="Seiyu Group">Seiyu Group</a> in Japan, and as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Best_Price&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Best Price (page does not exist)">Best Price</a> in India. It has wholly owned operations in Argentina, Brazil, and Canada. It also owns and operates the <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Club" title="Sam's Club">Sam's Club</a> <a href="/wiki/Warehouse_club" title="Warehouse club">retail warehouses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2015_Annual_Report_Page_19_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015_Annual_Report_Page_19-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Location_WorldMap_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Location_WorldMap-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Walmart is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_by_revenue" class="mw-redirect" title="List of companies by revenue">world's largest company by revenue</a>, according to the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Fortune Global 500</a> list in 2016, as well as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_employers" title="List of largest employers">largest private employer</a> in the world with 2.2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million employees. It is a <a href="/wiki/Family_business" title="Family business">family-owned business</a>, as the company is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Walton_family" title="Walton family">Walton family</a>. Sam Walton's heirs own over 50<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent of Walmart through their holding company, Walton Enterprises, and through their individual holdings.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Walmart is also one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_corporations_by_market_capitalization" class="mw-redirect" title="List of corporations by market capitalization">world's most valuable companies by market value</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> and is also the largest <a href="/wiki/Grocery_store" title="Grocery store">grocery</a> retailer in the U.S. In 2016, 62.3<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent of Walmart's <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>478.614<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span> sales came from its U.S. operations.<sup id="cite_ref-2016_Annual_Report_Page_20_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_Annual_Report_Page_20-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The company was listed on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a> in 1972. By 1988, Walmart was the most profitable retailer in the U.S.,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> and by October 1989, it had become the largest in terms of revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Geographically limited to the <a href="/wiki/American_South" class="mw-redirect" title="American South">South</a> and lower <a href="/wiki/American_Midwest" class="mw-redirect" title="American Midwest">Midwest</a> up to the mid-1980s, by the early-1990s, the company's presence spanned from coast to coast‍—‌Sam's Club opened in <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> in November 1989 and the first California outlet opened in <a href="/wiki/Lancaster,_California" title="Lancaster, California">Lancaster</a> in July 1990. A Walmart in <a href="/wiki/York,_Pennsylvania" title="York, Pennsylvania">York, Pennsylvania</a> opened in October 1990, bringing the main store to the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">Northeast</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Warner_90_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warner_90-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Walmart's investments outside North America have seen mixed results: its operations in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> are highly successful, whereas ventures in Germany and South Korea failed.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Walmart" title="History of Walmart">History of Walmart</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1945.E2.80.931969:_Early_history">1945–1969: Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1945–1969: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walton%27s_Five_and_Dime_store,_Bentonville,_Arkansas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Walton%27s_Five_and_Dime_store%2C_Bentonville%2C_Arkansas.jpg/220px-Walton%27s_Five_and_Dime_store%2C_Bentonville%2C_Arkansas.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Walton%27s_Five_and_Dime_store%2C_Bentonville%2C_Arkansas.jpg/330px-Walton%27s_Five_and_Dime_store%2C_Bentonville%2C_Arkansas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Walton%27s_Five_and_Dime_store%2C_Bentonville%2C_Arkansas.jpg/440px-Walton%27s_Five_and_Dime_store%2C_Bentonville%2C_Arkansas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walton%27s_Five_and_Dime_store,_Bentonville,_Arkansas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sam Walton's original Walton's <a href="/wiki/Five_and_dime" class="mw-redirect" title="Five and dime">Five and Dime</a> store in <a href="/wiki/Bentonville,_Arkansas" title="Bentonville, Arkansas">Bentonville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a> now serving as the Walmart Visitor Center</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1945, a businessman and a former <a href="/wiki/J._C._Penney" title="J. C. Penney">J.&#160;C. Penney</a> employee, <a href="/wiki/Sam_Walton" title="Sam Walton">Sam Walton</a>, purchased a branch of the <a href="/wiki/Ben_Franklin_(company)" title="Ben Franklin (company)">Ben Franklin</a> stores from the <a href="/wiki/Butler_Brothers" title="Butler Brothers">Butler Brothers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-madeinamerica_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-madeinamerica-18">[18]</a></sup> His primary focus was on selling products at low prices to get higher-volume sales at a lower <a href="/wiki/Profit_margin" title="Profit margin">profit margin</a>, portraying it as a crusade for the consumer. He experienced setbacks, because the lease price and branch purchase were unusually high, but he was able to find lower-cost suppliers than those used by other stores. He passed on the savings in the product pricing.<sup id="cite_ref-a_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a-19">[19]</a></sup> Sales increased 45<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent in his first year of ownership to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$105,000</span> in revenue, which increased to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$140,000</span> the next year and <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$175,000</span> the year after that. Within the fifth year, the store was generating <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$250,000</span> in revenue. When the lease for the location expired, Walton was unable to reach an agreement for renewal, so he opened up a new store at 105 N. Main Street in Bentonville, naming it "Walton's Five and Dime".<sup id="cite_ref-a_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BriefHistory_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BriefHistory-20">[20]</a></sup> That store is now the Walmart Museum.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmartlogo1.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Walmartlogo1.png/220px-Walmartlogo1.png" width="220" height="45" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5e/Walmartlogo1.png 1.5x" data-file-width="221" data-file-height="45" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmartlogo1.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Original logo, 1962–1964</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmartlogo2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Walmartlogo2.png/220px-Walmartlogo2.png" width="220" height="53" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/07/Walmartlogo2.png 1.5x" data-file-width="227" data-file-height="55" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmartlogo2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Logo used 1964–1981</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_logo_hyphen.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Walmart_logo_hyphen.png/220px-Walmart_logo_hyphen.png" width="220" height="32" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Walmart_logo_hyphen.png/330px-Walmart_logo_hyphen.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Walmart_logo_hyphen.png/440px-Walmart_logo_hyphen.png 2x" data-file-width="2711" data-file-height="394" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_logo_hyphen.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Logo used 1981–1992</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wal-Mart_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Wal-Mart_logo.svg/220px-Wal-Mart_logo.svg.png" width="220" height="31" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Wal-Mart_logo.svg/330px-Wal-Mart_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Wal-Mart_logo.svg/440px-Wal-Mart_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="303" data-file-height="43" /></a>

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wal-Mart_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Logo used 1992–2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:New_Walmart_Logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/New_Walmart_Logo.svg/220px-New_Walmart_Logo.svg.png" width="220" height="53" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/New_Walmart_Logo.svg/330px-New_Walmart_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/New_Walmart_Logo.svg/440px-New_Walmart_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="124" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:New_Walmart_Logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Logo used 2008–present<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On July 2, 1962, Walton opened the first Walmart Discount City store at 719<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>W. Walnut Street in <a href="/wiki/Rogers,_Arkansas" title="Rogers, Arkansas">Rogers, Arkansas</a>. The building is now occupied by a hardware store and an antique mall, while the company's "Store #1"‍—‌since relocated to a larger discount store and now expanded to a Supercenter‍—‌is located several blocks west at 2110 W. Walnut Street. Within its first five years, the company expanded to 24<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>stores across <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a> and reached <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$12.6<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span> in sales.<sup id="cite_ref-discountcity_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-discountcity-23">[23]</a></sup> In 1968, it opened its first stores outside Arkansas, in <a href="/wiki/Sikeston,_Missouri" title="Sikeston, Missouri">Sikeston, Missouri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Claremore,_Oklahoma" title="Claremore, Oklahoma">Claremore, Oklahoma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1969.E2.80.931990:_Incorporation_and_growth_as_a_regional_power">1969–1990: Incorporation and growth as a regional power</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1969–1990: Incorporation and growth as a regional power">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The company was <a href="/wiki/Incorporation_(business)" title="Incorporation (business)">incorporated</a> as <b>Wal-Mart Stores, Inc.</b> on October 31, 1969. In 1970, it opened its home office and first distribution center in <a href="/wiki/Bentonville,_Arkansas" title="Bentonville, Arkansas">Bentonville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>. It had 38<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>stores operating with 1,500 employees and sales of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$44.2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span>. It began trading stock as a <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">publicly held company</a> on October 1, 1970, and was soon listed on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a>. The first <a href="/wiki/Stock_split" title="Stock split">stock split</a> occurred in May 1971 at a price of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$47</span>. By this time, Walmart was operating in five states: Arkansas, Kansas, Louisiana, Missouri, and Oklahoma; it entered Tennessee in 1973 and Kentucky and Mississippi in 1974. As it moved into Texas in 1975, there were 125<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>stores with 7,500 employees and total sales of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$340.3<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-24">[24]</a></sup> Walmart opened its first Texas store in <a href="/wiki/Mount_Pleasant,_Texas" title="Mount Pleasant, Texas">Mount Pleasant</a> on November 11, 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-Halkias_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halkias-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 1980s, Walmart continued to grow rapidly, and by its 25th anniversary in 1987, there were 1,198 stores with sales of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$15.9<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span> and 200,000 associates.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-24">[24]</a></sup> This year also marked the completion of the company's satellite network, a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$24<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span> investment linking all operating units with the Bentonville office via two-way voice and data transmission and one-way video communication. At the time, it was the largest private satellite network, allowing the corporate office to track inventory and sales and to instantly communicate to stores.<sup id="cite_ref-satellite_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-satellite-26">[26]</a></sup> In 1988, Walton stepped down as CEO and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/David_Glass_(businessman)" title="David Glass (businessman)">David Glass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LA_Times_88_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Times_88-27">[27]</a></sup> Walton remained as Chairman of the Board.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:InsideWalmartWestPlains.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/InsideWalmartWestPlains.JPG/220px-InsideWalmartWestPlains.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/InsideWalmartWestPlains.JPG/330px-InsideWalmartWestPlains.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/InsideWalmartWestPlains.JPG/440px-InsideWalmartWestPlains.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:InsideWalmartWestPlains.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Inside the Walmart Supercenter in <a href="/wiki/West_Plains,_Missouri" title="West Plains, Missouri">West Plains, Missouri</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1988, the first Wal-Mart Supercenter opened in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_Missouri" title="Washington, Missouri">Washington, Missouri</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Krieg_14_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krieg_14-28">[28]</a></sup> Thanks to its superstores, it surpassed <a href="/wiki/Toys_%22R%22_Us" title="Toys &quot;R&quot; Us">Toys "R" Us</a> in toy sales in the late-1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-Byrnes_04_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Byrnes_04-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990.E2.80.932005:_Retail_rise_to_multinational_status">1990–2005: Retail rise to multinational status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1990–2005: Retail rise to multinational status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While it was the No. 3 retailer in the U.S., Walmart was more profitable than rivals Kmart and Sears by the late 1980s. By 1990, it became the largest U.S. retailer by revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-Hayes_90_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes_90-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prior to the summer of 1990, Walmart had no presence on the West Coast or in the Northeast (except for a single Sam's Club in New Jersey which opened in November 1989), but in July and October that year, it opened its first stores in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, respectively. By the mid-1990s, it was far and away the most powerful retailer in the U.S. and expanded into Mexico in 1991 and Canada in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Walmart stores opened throughout the rest of the U.S., with Vermont being the last state to get a store in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-PBS04_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBS04-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>The company also opened stores outside North America, entering South America in 1995 with stores in Argentina and Brazil; and Europe in July 1999, buying <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a> in the United Kingdom for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$10<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-IHT_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHT-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1998, Walmart introduced the Neighborhood Market concept with three stores in <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-grocerybiz_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grocerybiz-34">[34]</a></sup> By 2005, estimates indicate that the company controlled about 20 percent of the retail grocery and consumables business.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000, <a href="/wiki/Lee_Scott_(businessman)" title="Lee Scott (businessman)">H. Lee Scott</a> became Walmart's President and CEO, as the company's sales increased to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$165<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-2000sales_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2000sales-36">[36]</a></sup> In 2002, it was listed for the first time as America's largest corporation on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list, with revenues of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$219.8<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span> and profits of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$6.7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span>. It has remained there every year, except in 2006 and 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-2007-Fortune-500_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2007-Fortune-500-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2006-Fortune-500_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2006-Fortune-500-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, Walmart reported <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$312.4<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span> in sales, more than 6,200 facilities around the world&#160;–&#160;including 3,800 stores in the United States and 2,800 elsewhere, employing more than 1.6<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million associates. Its U.S. presence grew so rapidly that only small pockets of the country remained more than 60 miles (97 kilometres) from the nearest store.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>As Walmart rapidly expanded into the world's largest corporation, many critics worried about its effect on local communities, particularly small towns with many "<a href="/wiki/Small_business" title="Small business">mom and pop</a>" stores. There have been several studies on the economic impact of Walmart on small towns and local businesses, jobs, and taxpayers. In one, Kenneth Stone, a Professor of Economics at <a href="/wiki/Iowa_State_University" title="Iowa State University">Iowa State University</a>, found that some small towns can lose almost half of their retail trade within ten years of a Walmart store opening.<sup id="cite_ref-Rural_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rural-44">[44]</a></sup> However, in another study, he compared the changes to what small town shops had faced in the past&#160;–&#160;including the development of the railroads, the advent of the Sears Roebuck catalog, as well as the arrival of shopping malls&#160;–&#160;and concluded that shop owners who adapt to changes in the retail market can thrive after Walmart arrives.<sup id="cite_ref-Rural_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rural-44">[44]</a></sup> A later study in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_State_University" title="Mississippi State University">Mississippi State University</a> showed that there are "both positive and negative impacts on existing stores in the area where the new supercenter locates."<sup id="cite_ref-Stone_Artz_Myles_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stone_Artz_Myles-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the aftermath of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> in September 2005, Walmart used its logistics network to organize a rapid response to the disaster, donating <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$20<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span> in cash, 1,500 truckloads of merchandise, food for 100,000 meals, as well as the promise of a job for every one of its displaced workers.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> An independent study by Steven Horwitz of <a href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_University" title="St. Lawrence University">St. Lawrence University</a> found that Walmart, <a href="/wiki/The_Home_Depot" title="The Home Depot">The Home Depot</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lowe%27s" title="Lowe's">Lowe's</a> made use of their local knowledge about supply chains, infrastructure, decision makers and other resources to provide emergency supplies and reopen stores well before FEMA began its response.<sup id="cite_ref-Kouzes_10_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kouzes_10-47">[47]</a></sup> While the company was overall lauded for its quick response&#160;– amidst <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_government_response_to_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Criticism of government response to Hurricane Katrina">criticism</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a>&#160;– several critics were nonetheless quick to point out that there still remained issues with the company's labor relations.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2005.E2.80.932010:_Initiatives">2005–2010: Initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2005–2010: Initiatives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Solar_Panels_on_Caguas,_Puerto_Rico_Walmart.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Solar_Panels_on_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico_Walmart.jpg/220px-Solar_Panels_on_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico_Walmart.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Solar_Panels_on_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico_Walmart.jpg/330px-Solar_Panels_on_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico_Walmart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Solar_Panels_on_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico_Walmart.jpg/440px-Solar_Panels_on_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico_Walmart.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2198" data-file-height="1318" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Solar_Panels_on_Caguas,_Puerto_Rico_Walmart.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Solar modules mounted on a Walmart Supercenter in <a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas, Puerto Rico</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In October 2005, Walmart announced several environmental measures to increase <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">energy efficiency</a>. The primary goals included spending <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$500<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span> a year to increase fuel efficiency in Walmart's truck fleet by 25 percent over three years and double it within ten, reduce <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions by 20 percent in seven years, reduce energy use at stores by 30 percent, and cut solid waste from U.S. stores and Sam's Clubs by 25 percent in three years. CEO Lee Scott said that Walmart's goal was to be a "good steward for the environment" and ultimately use only <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> sources and produce zero waste.<sup id="cite_ref-going_green_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-going_green-49">[49]</a></sup> The company also designed three new experimental stores with <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">wind turbines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic">photovoltaic</a> solar panels, <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuel</a>-capable boilers, water-cooled refrigerators, and <a href="/wiki/Xeriscaping" title="Xeriscaping">xeriscape</a> gardens.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Despite much criticism of its environmental record, Walmart took a few steps in what some viewed as a positive direction, which included becoming the biggest seller of organic milk and the biggest buyer of organic cotton in the world, as well as reducing packaging and energy costs.<sup id="cite_ref-GuntherMark_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuntherMark-51">[51]</a></sup> Walmart also spent nearly a year working with outside consultants to discover the company's total environmental impact and find areas for improvement. Walmart has also recently created its own <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_industry" title="Electric power industry">electric company</a> in Texas, <i>Texas Retail Energy</i>, and plans to supply its stores with cheap power purchased at wholesale prices. Through this new venture, the company expects to save <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$15<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span> annually and also to lay the groundwork and infrastructure to sell electricity to Texas consumers in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-redorbit_electricity_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-redorbit_electricity-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2006, Walmart sought to appeal to a more affluent demographic. The company launched a new Supercenter concept in <a href="/wiki/Plano,_Texas" title="Plano, Texas">Plano, Texas</a>, intended to compete against stores seen as more upscale and appealing, such as <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The new store has wood floors, wider aisles, a <a href="/wiki/Sushi" title="Sushi">sushi</a> bar, a coffee/sandwich shop with free <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a> Internet access, and more expensive beers, wines, electronics, and other goods. The exterior has a hunter green background behind the Walmart letters, similar to Neighborhood Market by Walmarts, instead of the blue previously used at its supercenters.</p>
<p>On September 12, 2007, Walmart introduced new advertising with the <a href="/wiki/Slogan" title="Slogan">slogan</a>, "<i>Save money. Live better.</i>", replacing "<i>Always Low Prices, Always</i>", which it had used for the previous 19 years. <a href="/wiki/Global_Insight" title="Global Insight">Global Insight</a>, which conducted the research that supported the ads, found that Walmart's <a href="/wiki/Price_level" title="Price level">price level</a> reduction resulted in savings for consumers of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$287<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span> in 2006, which equated to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$957</span> per person or <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2,500</span> per household (up 7.3 percent from the 2004 savings estimate of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2,329</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_at_5152_Canoga_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Walmart_at_5152_Canoga_Park.jpg/220px-Walmart_at_5152_Canoga_Park.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Walmart_at_5152_Canoga_Park.jpg/330px-Walmart_at_5152_Canoga_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Walmart_at_5152_Canoga_Park.jpg/440px-Walmart_at_5152_Canoga_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_at_5152_Canoga_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The exterior of the Walmart discount store in <a href="/wiki/West_Hills,_Los_Angeles" title="West Hills, Los Angeles">West Hills, Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On June 30, 2008, Walmart removed the hyphen from its logo and replaced the star with a <i>Spark</i> symbol that resembles a sunburst, flower, or star. The new logo received mixed reviews from design critics, who questioned whether the new logo was as bold as those of competitors, such as the <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a> bullseye or as instantly recognizable as the previous company logo, which was used for 18 years.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The new logo made its debut on the company's website on July 1, 2008. Walmart's U.S. locations were to update store logos in the fall of 2008, as part of an ongoing evolution of its brand.<sup id="cite_ref-new_logo_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_logo-57">[57]</a></sup> Walmart Canada started to adopt the logo for its stores in early 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 20, 2009, Walmart announced that it was paying a combined <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$933.6<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span> in bonuses to every full and part-time hourly worker.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> This was in addition to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$788.8<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span> in <a href="/wiki/Profit_sharing" title="Profit sharing">profit sharing</a>, <a href="/wiki/401(k)" title="401(k)">401(k)</a> pension contributions, hundreds of millions of dollars in merchandise discounts, and contributions to the employees' stock purchase plan.<sup id="cite_ref-Maestri_09_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maestri_09-60">[60]</a></sup> While the economy at large was in an ongoing <a href="/wiki/Recession" title="Recession">recession</a>, Walmart, the largest retailer in the U.S., reported solid financial figures for the most recent fiscal year (ending January 31, 2009), with <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$401.2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span> in net sales, a gain of 7.2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent from the prior year. Income from continuing operations increased 3<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$13.3<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span>, and earnings per share rose 6<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$3.35</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>On February 22, 2010, the company confirmed it was acquiring <a href="/wiki/Streaming_media" title="Streaming media">video streaming</a> company <a href="/wiki/Vudu,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Vudu, Inc.">Vudu, Inc.</a> for an estimated <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$100<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011.E2.80.93present:_Current_developments">2011–present: Current developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2011–present: Current developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart%E2%80%99s_Grease_Fuel_Truck.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Walmart%E2%80%99s_Grease_Fuel_Truck.jpg/220px-Walmart%E2%80%99s_Grease_Fuel_Truck.jpg" width="220" height="57" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Walmart%E2%80%99s_Grease_Fuel_Truck.jpg/330px-Walmart%E2%80%99s_Grease_Fuel_Truck.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Walmart%E2%80%99s_Grease_Fuel_Truck.jpg/440px-Walmart%E2%80%99s_Grease_Fuel_Truck.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2464" data-file-height="642" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart%E2%80%99s_Grease_Fuel_Truck.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Truck converted to run on biofuel</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Walmart's truck fleet logs millions of miles each year, and the company planned to double the fleet's efficiency between 2005 and 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The truck below is one of 15 based at Walmart's <a href="/wiki/Buckeye,_Arizona" title="Buckeye, Arizona">Buckeye, Arizona</a>, distribution center that was converted to run on a type of <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuel</a> made from reclaimed cooking grease produced during food preparation at Walmart stores.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></li>
<li>In January 2011, Walmart announced a program to improve the nutritional value of its store brands over five years, gradually reducing the amount of salt and sugar and eliminating <a href="/wiki/Trans_fat" title="Trans fat">trans fat</a>. Walmart also promised to negotiate with suppliers with respect to nutritional issues, reduce prices for whole foods and vegetables, and open stores in low-income areas, so-called "<a href="/wiki/Food_desert" title="Food desert">food deserts</a>", where there are no supermarkets.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li>On April 23, 2011, the company announced that it was testing its new "Walmart To Go" home delivery system where customers will be able to order specific items offered on their website. The initial test was in <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose, California</a>, and the company has not yet said whether the delivery system will be rolled out nationwide.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_11_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_11-66">[66]</a></sup> On November 14, 2012, Walmart launched its first mail subscription service called Goodies. Customers pay a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$7</span> monthly subscription for five to eight delivered food samples each month, so they can try new foods.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li>In August 2013, the firm announced it was in talks to acquire a majority stake in the <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>-based supermarket chain, <a href="/wiki/Naivas" class="mw-redirect" title="Naivas">Naivas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></li>
<li>In June 2014, some Walmart employees went on strike in major U.S. cities demanding higher wages.<sup id="cite_ref-CNNMoney_Walmart_2014-06-04_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNNMoney_Walmart_2014-06-04-69">[69]</a></sup></li>
<li>In July 2014, American actor and comedian <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Morgan" title="Tracy Morgan">Tracy Morgan</a> launched a lawsuit against Walmart seeking punitive damages over a multi-car pile-up which the suit alleges was caused by the driver of one of the firm's tractor-trailers who had not slept for 24 hours. Morgan's limousine was apparently hit by the trailer, injuring him and two fellow passengers and killing a fourth, fellow comedian James McNair.<sup id="cite_ref-MorganWalmart_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MorganWalmart-70">[70]</a></sup> Walmart settled with the McNair family for $10 million, while admitting no liability.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Morgan and Walmart reached a settlement in 2015 for an undisclosed amount,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> though Walmart later accused its insurers of "bad faith" in refusing to pay the settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2015, the company closed five stores on short notice for plumbing repairs.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> However, employees and the <a href="/wiki/United_Food_and_Commercial_Workers_International_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="United Food and Commercial Workers International Union">United Food and Commercial Workers International Union</a> (UFCW) alleged some stores were closed in retaliation for strikes aimed at increasing wages and improving working conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The UFCW filed a complaint with the <a href="/wiki/National_Labor_Relations_Board" title="National Labor Relations Board">National Labor Relations Board</a>. All five stores have since reopened.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></li>
<li>On October 14, 2015, Walmart saw its stock fall 10 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>On January 15, 2016, Walmart announced it will close 269 stores in 2016, affecting 16,000 workers.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> 154 out of the 269 stores earmarked for closure are in the U.S. (150 Walmart U.S. stores, 115 Walmart International stores, and 4<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Sam's Clubs). 95 percent of these U.S. stores are located, on average, 10 miles from another Walmart store.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-79">[79]</a></sup> The 269 stores represent less than 1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent of global square footage and revenue. Walmart Express, of which all 102 locations are included in the closures, had been in a pilot program since 2011. In light of these closings, Walmart plans to focus on "strengthening Supercenters, optimizing Neighborhood Markets, growing the e-commerce business and expanding pickup services for customers". In fiscal 2017, the company plans to open between 50 and 60 Supercenters, 85 to 95 Neighborhood Markets, 7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>to 10 Sam's Clubs, and 200 to 240 international locations.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-79">[79]</a></sup> At the end of fiscal 2016, Walmart opened 38 Supercenters and relocated, expanded or converted 21 discount stores into Supercenters, for a total of 59 Supercenters, opened 69 Neighborhood Markets, opened 8 Sam's Clubs, and opened 173 international locations and relocated, expanded or converted 4 locations for a total of 177 international locations.</li>
<li>In 2015, Walmart was the biggest US commercial producer of <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a> with 142 <a href="/wiki/Megawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt">MW</a> <a href="/wiki/Nameplate_capacity" title="Nameplate capacity">capacity</a>, and has 17 <a href="/wiki/Energy_storage" title="Energy storage">energy storage</a> projects.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></li>
<li>On August 8, 2016, Walmart announced a deal to acquire e-commerce website <a href="/wiki/Jet.com" title="Jet.com">Jet.com</a> for US$3.3 billion<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Jet.com co-founder and <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">CEO</a> <a href="/wiki/Marc_Lore" title="Marc Lore">Marc Lore</a> will stay on to run Jet.com in addition to Walmart's existing U.S. e-commerce operation. The acquisition is structured as a payout of $3 billion in cash, and an additional $300 million in Walmart stock vested over time as part of an incentive bonus plan for Jet.com executives.</li>
<li>October 19, 2016, Walmart announced it would partner up with IBM (IBM) and Tsinghua University to track the pork supply chain in China using blockchain.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></li>
<li>February 15, 2017, Walmart announced acquisition of Moosejaw, a leading online active outdoor retailer, for approximately $51 million. The acquisition closed on Feb. 13, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Growing_crime_problem">Growing crime problem</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Growing crime problem">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Police reports from dozens of Walmart stores suggest the number of petty crimes committed on Walmart properties nationwide in 2016 will be in the hundreds of thousands. Additionally, more than 200 violent crimes, including attempted kidnappings and multiple stabbings, shootings, and murders, have occurred at the nation’s 4,500 Walmarts as of August 2016, or about one a day, according to an analysis of media reports. Walmart has taken steps to ameliorate the problem, but critics say that effective action will require it to spend more on security and employees.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operating_divisions">Operating divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Operating divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_footprint.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Walmart_footprint.png/220px-Walmart_footprint.png" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Walmart_footprint.png/330px-Walmart_footprint.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Walmart_footprint.png/440px-Walmart_footprint.png 2x" data-file-width="1859" data-file-height="968" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_footprint.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Walmart stores in the U.S., as of August 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_assets_owned_by_Walmart" title="List of assets owned by Walmart">List of assets owned by Walmart</a></div>
<p>Walmart's operations are organized into four divisions: Walmart U.S., Walmart International, <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Club" title="Sam's Club">Sam's Club</a> and Global eCommerce.<sup id="cite_ref-annrep_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annrep-87">[87]</a></sup> The company offers various retail formats throughout these divisions, including supercenters, supermarkets, hypermarkets, warehouse clubs, cash-and-carry stores, home improvement, specialty electronics, restaurants, apparel stores, drugstores, convenience stores, and digital retail.<sup id="cite_ref-2016_Annual_Report_Page_19_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_Annual_Report_Page_19-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Walmart_U.S.">Walmart U.S.</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Walmart U.S.">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Walmart U.S.</b> is the company's largest division, accounting for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$298.378<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span>, or 62.3 percent of total sales, for fiscal 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-2016_Annual_Report_Page_20_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_Annual_Report_Page_20-14">[14]</a></sup> It consists of three retail formats that have become commonplace in the United States: <a href="/wiki/Hypermarket" title="Hypermarket">Supercenters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Discount_store" title="Discount store">Discount Stores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walmart_Neighborhood_Market" class="mw-redirect" title="Walmart Neighborhood Market">Neighborhood Markets</a>, and other small formats. The discount stores sell a variety of mostly non-grocery products, though emphasis has now shifted towards supercenters, which include more groceries. As of January 31, 2017, there are a total of 4,672 Walmart U.S. stores.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The president and CEO of Walmart U.S. is Greg Foran.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Walmart_Supercenter">Walmart Supercenter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Walmart Supercenter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_in_NRH,_Texas.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Walmart_in_NRH%2C_Texas.png/220px-Walmart_in_NRH%2C_Texas.png" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Walmart_in_NRH%2C_Texas.png/330px-Walmart_in_NRH%2C_Texas.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Walmart_in_NRH%2C_Texas.png/440px-Walmart_in_NRH%2C_Texas.png 2x" data-file-width="2038" data-file-height="1284" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_in_NRH,_Texas.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Walmart Supercenter in <a href="/wiki/North_Richland_Hills,_Texas" title="North Richland Hills, Texas">North Richland Hills, Texas</a> that opened in 1991 as a discount store, later expanded to a supercenter, sporting a new paint job taken in June 2016.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Walmart Supercenters</b>, simply branded as "Walmart", are <a href="/wiki/Hypermarket" title="Hypermarket">hypermarkets</a> with sizes varying from 69,000 to 260,000 square feet (6,400 to 24,200 square meters), but averaging about 187,000 square feet (17,400 square meters).<sup id="cite_ref-annrep_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annrep-87">[87]</a></sup> These stock general merchandise and a full-service supermarket, including meat and poultry, <a href="/wiki/Baking" title="Baking">baked goods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delicatessen" title="Delicatessen">delicatessen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frozen_food" title="Frozen food">frozen foods</a>, dairy products, garden <a href="/wiki/Produce" title="Produce">produce</a>, and fresh seafood. Many Walmart Supercenters also have a garden center, <a href="/wiki/Pet_store" title="Pet store">pet shop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharmacy" title="Pharmacy">pharmacy</a>, Tire &amp; <a href="/wiki/Oil_change" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil change">Lube</a> Express, optical center, one-hour photo processing lab, portrait studio, and numerous alcove shops, such as cellular phone stores, hair and nail salons, video rental stores, local bank branches (newer locations have <a href="/wiki/Woodforest_National_Bank" title="Woodforest National Bank">Woodforest National Bank</a> branches), and fast food outlets, those usually being <a href="/wiki/Subway_(restaurant)" title="Subway (restaurant)">Subway</a> but sometimes <a href="/wiki/Dunkin%27_Donuts" title="Dunkin' Donuts">Dunkin' Donuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wendy%27s" title="Wendy's">Wendy's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Checkers_(fast_food)" class="mw-redirect" title="Checkers (fast food)">Checker's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Auntie_Annes" class="mw-redirect" title="Auntie Annes">Auntie Annes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Hortons" title="Tim Hortons">Tim Hortons</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Blimpie" title="Blimpie">Blimpie</a>. Many featured <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> restaurants, but in 2007, Walmart announced it would stop opening McDonald's restaurants at most of their newer stores. Most locations that opened up after the announcement had Subway as their restaurants, and some McDonald's inside the stores were replaced with <a href="/wiki/Subway_(restaurant)" title="Subway (restaurant)">Subways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> In some Canadian locations, Tim Hortons were opened. Some<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Some locations also have fuel stations which sell gasoline distributed by <a href="/wiki/Murphy_USA" title="Murphy USA">Murphy USA</a> (which spun off from <a href="/wiki/Murphy_Oil" title="Murphy Oil">Murphy Oil</a> in 2013), <a href="/wiki/Sunoco,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Sunoco, Inc.">Sunoco, Inc.</a> ("Optima"), the <a href="/wiki/Tesoro" title="Tesoro">Tesoro</a> Corporation ("Mirastar"), USA Gasoline, and even now Walmart-branded gas stations.<sup id="cite_ref-CSNews_WMGas_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSNews_WMGas-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first Supercenter opened in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_Missouri" title="Washington, Missouri">Washington, Missouri</a>, in 1988. A similar concept, <i><a href="/wiki/Hypermart_USA" title="Hypermart USA">Hypermart USA</a></i>, had opened in <a href="/wiki/Garland,_Texas" title="Garland, Texas">Garland, Texas</a>, a year earlier. All Hypermart USA stores were later closed or converted into Supercenters.</p>
<p>As of January 31, 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 3,522 Walmart Supercenters in 49 of the 50 U.S. states, the District of Columbia, and Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> Hawaii is the only state to not have a Supercenter location. The largest Supercenter in the United States, covering 260,000 square feet (24,000 square meters) on two floors, is located in <a href="/wiki/Crossgates_Commons" title="Crossgates Commons">Crossgates Commons</a> in <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany, New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> In 2006, the busiest in the world was the one in <a href="/wiki/Rapid_City,_South_Dakota" title="Rapid City, South Dakota">Rapid City, South Dakota</a>.</p>
<p>The "Supercenter" portion of the name has since been phased out, with these stores now simply referred to as "Walmart", since the company introduced the new Walmart logo in 2008. The <i>Supercentre</i> name is still used in Canada, where the company opened its 100th Canadian store in 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> some of them former <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Club" title="Sam's Club">Sam's Club</a> locations.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Walmart_Discount_Store">Walmart Discount Store</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Walmart Discount Store">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wal-Mart_Albemarle_Rd_Charlotte,_NC_(7580001150).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Wal-Mart_Albemarle_Rd_Charlotte%2C_NC_%287580001150%29.jpg/220px-Wal-Mart_Albemarle_Rd_Charlotte%2C_NC_%287580001150%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Wal-Mart_Albemarle_Rd_Charlotte%2C_NC_%287580001150%29.jpg/330px-Wal-Mart_Albemarle_Rd_Charlotte%2C_NC_%287580001150%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Wal-Mart_Albemarle_Rd_Charlotte%2C_NC_%287580001150%29.jpg/440px-Wal-Mart_Albemarle_Rd_Charlotte%2C_NC_%287580001150%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wal-Mart_Albemarle_Rd_Charlotte,_NC_(7580001150).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The exterior of the Walmart Discount Store in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte, North Carolina</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bellingham_Walmart.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Bellingham_Walmart.jpg/220px-Bellingham_Walmart.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Bellingham_Walmart.jpg/330px-Bellingham_Walmart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Bellingham_Walmart.jpg/440px-Bellingham_Walmart.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="717" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bellingham_Walmart.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The exterior of a multi-entrance Walmart Discount Store in <a href="/wiki/Bellingham,_Washington" title="Bellingham, Washington">Bellingham, Washington</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Walmart Discount Stores</b>, also branded as simply "Walmart", are <a href="/wiki/Discount_store" title="Discount store">discount department stores</a> with sizes varying from 30,000 to 206,000 square feet (2,800 to 19,100 square meters), with the average store covering about 104,000 square feet (9,700 square meters).<sup id="cite_ref-annrep_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annrep-87">[87]</a></sup> They carry <a href="/wiki/General_merchandise" class="mw-redirect" title="General merchandise">general merchandise</a> and limited <a href="/wiki/Grocery" class="mw-redirect" title="Grocery">groceries</a>. Some newer and remodeled discount stores have an expanded grocery department, similar to Target's PFresh department. Many of these stores also feature a garden center, <a href="/wiki/Pharmacy" title="Pharmacy">pharmacy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tire" title="Tire">tire</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Motor_oil" title="Motor oil">Lube</a> Express, optical center, <a href="/wiki/Photographic_processing" title="Photographic processing">one-hour photo processing lab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portrait" title="Portrait">portrait</a> studio, a bank branch, a cell phone store, and a fast food outlet, usually <a href="/wiki/Subway_(restaurant)" title="Subway (restaurant)">Subway</a> or <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> or <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a>. Some also have gasoline stations.<sup id="cite_ref-CSNews_WMGas_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSNews_WMGas-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1990, Walmart opened its first <i>Bud's Discount City</i> location in Bentonville. Bud's operated as a closeout store, much like <a href="/wiki/Big_Lots" title="Big Lots">Big Lots</a>. Many locations were opened to fulfill leases in shopping centers as Walmart stores left and moved into newly built Supercenters. All of the Bud's Discount City stores closed or converted into Walmart Discount Stores by 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-DSN_Retailing_Today_97_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DSN_Retailing_Today_97-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of January 31, 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 415 Walmart Discount Stores in 41 states and Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> Idaho, Montana, Nebraska, North Dakota, South Carolina, South Dakota, Utah, District of Columbia, West Virginia, and Wyoming are the only states and territories where a discount store does not operate.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Walmart_Neighborhood_Market">Walmart Neighborhood Market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Walmart Neighborhood Market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WalMartNeighborhoodMarketHoustonHillcroft.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/WalMartNeighborhoodMarketHoustonHillcroft.JPG/220px-WalMartNeighborhoodMarketHoustonHillcroft.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/WalMartNeighborhoodMarketHoustonHillcroft.JPG/330px-WalMartNeighborhoodMarketHoustonHillcroft.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/WalMartNeighborhoodMarketHoustonHillcroft.JPG/440px-WalMartNeighborhoodMarketHoustonHillcroft.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WalMartNeighborhoodMarketHoustonHillcroft.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Walmart Neighborhood Market in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, Texas</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Walmart Neighborhood Market</b> is a chain of <a href="/wiki/Grocery_store" title="Grocery store">grocery stores</a> with sizes varying from 28,000 to 66,000 square feet (2,600 to 6,100 square meters), with an average size of 42,000 square feet (3,900 square meters).<sup id="cite_ref-annrep_87-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annrep-87">[87]</a></sup> They are used to fill the gap between supercenters, infilling areas where another supermarket chain had closed all stores due to competition from Walmart Supercenters. These Markets offer a variety of products including full lines of groceries, pharmaceuticals, health and beauty aids, photo developing services, and a limited selection of <a href="/wiki/General_merchandise" class="mw-redirect" title="General merchandise">general merchandise</a>. The first store opened in 1998, in <a href="/wiki/Bentonville,_Arkansas" title="Bentonville, Arkansas">Bentonville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>. As of January 31, 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 699 Walmart Neighborhood Markets.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> Neighborhood Markets and other small formats operate in 31 states and Puerto Rico (under the Amigo banner). Alaska, Delaware, Hawaii, Iowa, Maine, Maryland, Massachusetts, Michigan, Minnesota, Montana, New Hampshire, New Jersey, North Dakota, Ohio, Pennsylvania, Rhode Island, South Dakota,Vermont, District of Columbia, and Wyoming are the only states and territories where Neighborhood Markets and other small formats do not operate.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_stores_and_concepts">Former stores and concepts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Former stores and concepts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Neighborhood_Market,_Alma.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Walmart_Neighborhood_Market%2C_Alma.JPG/220px-Walmart_Neighborhood_Market%2C_Alma.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Walmart_Neighborhood_Market%2C_Alma.JPG/330px-Walmart_Neighborhood_Market%2C_Alma.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Walmart_Neighborhood_Market%2C_Alma.JPG/440px-Walmart_Neighborhood_Market%2C_Alma.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5152" data-file-height="3864" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Neighborhood_Market,_Alma.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2015 photo of a Walmart Express branded as a Walmart Neighborhood Market in <a href="/wiki/Alma,_Georgia" title="Alma, Georgia">Alma, Georgia</a> that closed in 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SupermercadodeWalmartHouston.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/SupermercadodeWalmartHouston.JPG/220px-SupermercadodeWalmartHouston.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/SupermercadodeWalmartHouston.JPG/330px-SupermercadodeWalmartHouston.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/SupermercadodeWalmartHouston.JPG/440px-SupermercadodeWalmartHouston.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SupermercadodeWalmartHouston.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2009 photo of the now-closed Supermercado de Walmart in <a href="/wiki/Spring_Branch,_Houston" title="Spring Branch, Houston">Spring Branch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WNMSB.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/WNMSB.jpg/220px-WNMSB.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/WNMSB.jpg/330px-WNMSB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/WNMSB.jpg/440px-WNMSB.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WNMSB.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Walmart Neighborhood Market in San Bernardino, California, parcel now vacant.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Walmart opened <b>"Supermercado de Walmart"</b> locations to appeal to <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic</a> communities in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The first one, a 39,000 square feet (3,600 square meters) store in the <a href="/wiki/Spring_Branch,_Houston" title="Spring Branch, Houston">Spring Branch</a> area of <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, opened on April 29, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-HoustonChron_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HoustonChron-95">[95]</a></sup> The store was a conversion of an existing Walmart Neighborhood Market.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> The opening was Walmart's first entry in the Hispanic grocery market in Houston.<sup id="cite_ref-Walsh_09_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walsh_09-97">[97]</a></sup> In 2009, another Supermercado de Walmart opened in <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Both the two Supermercado de Walmart locations have closed in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> In 2009, Walmart opened "Mas Club", a warehouse retail operation patterned after <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Club" title="Sam's Club">Sam's Club</a>. It closed its doors in 2014 with only one store<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-HoustonChron_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HoustonChron-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p><b>Walmart Express</b> was a chain of smaller discount stores, with a range of services, from groceries to check cashing and gasoline service. The concept was focused on small towns deemed not able to support a larger store, and large cities where space was at a premium. Walmart planned to build 15 to 20 Walmart Express stores, focusing on Arkansas, North Carolina and Chicago, by the end of its fiscal year in January 2012. As of September 8, 2014, Walmart re-branded all of its Express format stores to Neighborhood Markets in an effort to streamline its retail offer. It continued to open new Express stores under the Neighborhood Market name. As of January 31, 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 36 small-format stores in the United States. These include Amigo (19 locations), Walmart on Campus (14 locations), and Walmart To Go (3 locations), a chain of gas station/convenience stores.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> As of January 15, 2016, Walmart announced that it will be closing 269 stores globally, including all 102 U.S. Walmart Express stores, including those branded as Neighborhood Markets.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Initiatives">Initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Initiatives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In September 2006, Walmart announced a pilot program to sell <a href="/wiki/Generic_drug" title="Generic drug">generic drugs</a> at <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$4</span><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>per prescription. The program was launched at stores in the <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">Tampa, Florida</a>, area, and by January 2007 had been expanded to all stores in Florida. While the average price of generics is<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><span style="white-space: nowrap">US$29</span> per prescription, compared to<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><span style="white-space: nowrap">US$102</span> for name-brand drugs, Walmart maintains that it is not selling at a loss, or providing them as an act of charity‍—‌instead, they are using the same mechanisms of mass distribution that it uses to bring lower prices to other products.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Many of Walmart's low cost generics are imported from India, where they are made by drug makers that include <a href="/wiki/Ranbaxy_Laboratories" title="Ranbaxy Laboratories">Ranbaxy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cipla" title="Cipla">Cipla</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>On February 6, 2007, the company launched a "beta" version of a movie download service, which sold about 3,000 films and television episodes from all major studios and television networks.<sup id="cite_ref-moviedownload_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moviedownload-103">[103]</a></sup> The service was discontinued on December 21, 2007, due to low sales.<sup id="cite_ref-moviedownloaddiscontinued_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moviedownloaddiscontinued-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 2008 through 2011, Walmart operated a pilot program in the small grocery store concept called <i>Marketside</i> in the metropolitan <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>, area. The company plans to incorporate what it has learned from this concept into its Walmart Express stores.<sup id="cite_ref-Jarman_Max_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jarman_Max-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Walmart began testing a free grocery pickup service, allowing customers to select products online and choose their pickup time. At the store, a Walmart employee loads the groceries into the customer's car. As of September 2015, the program has expanded to 13 U.S. cities, and the company expects more stores to begin offering this service.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2016, Walmart announced a change to ShippingPass, its three-day shipping service, and that it will move from a three-day delivery to two-day delivery to remain competitive with Amazon.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Walmart priced it at 49 dollars per year, compared to Amazon Prime's 99 dollar per year price. If you are already a subscriber you get one month free.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2016, Walmart and Sam's Club announced they will begin testing last-mile grocery delivery that uses services including <a href="/wiki/Uber_(company)" title="Uber (company)">Uber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyft" title="Lyft">Lyft</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Deliv" title="Deliv">Deliv</a>, to bring customers' orders to their homes. Walmart customers will be able to shop using the company's online grocery service at grocery.walmart.com, then request delivery at checkout for a small fee. The first tests will go live in Denver and Phoenix.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Walmart_International">Walmart International</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Walmart International">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WalMart_international_locations.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/WalMart_international_locations.svg/220px-WalMart_international_locations.svg.png" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/WalMart_international_locations.svg/330px-WalMart_international_locations.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/WalMart_international_locations.svg/440px-WalMart_international_locations.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="863" data-file-height="443" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WalMart_international_locations.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
