Walmart international locations. Former locations are shown in red.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of January 31, 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Walmart's international operations comprised 6,363 stores<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> and 800,000 workers in 26<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>countries outside the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Walmart_international_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walmart_international-111">[111]</a></sup> There are wholly owned operations in Argentina, Brazil, Canada, and the UK. With 2.2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million employees worldwide, the company is the largest private employer in the U.S. and Mexico, and one of the largest in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-OurBusiness_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OurBusiness-6">[6]</a></sup> In fiscal 2016, Walmart's international division sales were <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$123.408<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span>, or 25.8<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent of total sales.<sup id="cite_ref-2016_Annual_Report_Page_20_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_Annual_Report_Page_20-14">[14]</a></sup> International retail units range from 4,000 to 185,000 square feet (370 to 17,190 square metres), wholesale units range from 35,000 to 70,000 square feet (3,300 to 6,500 square metres) and other units (including drugstores and convenience stores) range up to 2,400 square feet (220 square metres).</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_America">Latin America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Latin America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As of January 31, 2017, there are a total of 4,097 locations in Latin America, which consists of locations in Argentina, Brazil, Chile, Costa Rica, El<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Salvador, Guatemala, Honduras, Mexico, and Nicaragua.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Argentina">Argentina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Argentina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Walmart Argentina was founded in 1995 and, as of November 30, 2016, operates 107 stores under the banners Walmart Supercenter (32 locations), Changomas (51 locations), Changomas Express (10 locations), Mi Changomas (8 locations), and Walmart Supermercado (6 locations).<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hiper_Bompre%C3%A7o.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Hiper_Bompre%C3%A7o.JPG/220px-Hiper_Bompre%C3%A7o.JPG" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Hiper_Bompre%C3%A7o.JPG/330px-Hiper_Bompre%C3%A7o.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Hiper_Bompre%C3%A7o.JPG/440px-Hiper_Bompre%C3%A7o.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="278" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hiper_Bompre%C3%A7o.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bompre%C3%A7o" title="Bompreço">Bompreço</a> in <a href="/wiki/Natal,_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Natal, Brazil">Natal, Brazil</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2004, Walmart bought the 118<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>stores in the <a href="/wiki/Bompre%C3%A7o" title="Bompreço">Bompreço</a> supermarket chain in northeastern Brazil. In late 2005, it took control of the Brazilian operations of Sonae Distribution Group through its new subsidiary, WMS Supermercados do Brasil, thus acquiring control of the Nacional and Mercadorama supermarket chains, the leaders in the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">Rio Grande do Sul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_(state)" title="Paraná (state)">Paraná</a> states, respectively. None of these stores were rebranded. As of January 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Walmart operated 61 Super-Bompreço stores, 39<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Hiper-Bompreço stores. It also ran 57<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Walmart Supercenters, 27<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Sam's Clubs, and 174 Todo Dia stores. With the acquisition of Bompreço and Sonae, by 2010, Walmart was the third largest supermarket chain in Brazil, behind <a href="/wiki/Carrefour" title="Carrefour">Carrefour</a> and <a href="/wiki/GPA_(company)" title="GPA (company)">Pão de Açúcar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WalmartBrazil_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WalmartBrazil-112">[112]</a></sup> Walmart Brasil, the operating company, has its head office in <a href="/wiki/Barueri" title="Barueri">Barueri</a>, São Paulo State, and regional offices in <a href="/wiki/Curitiba" title="Curitiba">Curitiba</a>, Paraná; <a href="/wiki/Porto_Alegre" title="Porto Alegre">Porto Alegre</a>, Rio Grande do Sul; <a href="/wiki/Recife" title="Recife">Recife</a>, Pernambuco; and <a href="/wiki/Salvador,_Bahia" title="Salvador, Bahia">Salvador</a>, Bahia.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> As of January 31, 2017, Walmart Brasil operates 498<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>stores under the banners Walmart Supercenter (55 locations), Sam's Club (27 locations), Todo Dia (150 locations), Supermercado Todo Dia (3 locations), Hypermarket (Bompreço) (38 locations), Supermarket (Bompreço) (59 locations), Mercadorama (Sonae) (13 locations), BIG (Sonae) (37 locations), Maxxi Atacado (Sonae) (44 locations), Nacional (Sonae) (55 locations), Walmart Posto (Gas Station) (14 locations), and Hiper Todo Dia (3 locations).<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_America">Central America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Central America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Walmart also owns 51<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent of the Central American Retail Holding Company (CARHCO), which as of January 31, 2017, consists of 220 stores in Guatemala (under the Paiz (25 locations), Walmart Supercenter (10 locations), Despensa Familiar (153 locations), and Maxi Dispensa (32 locations) banners),<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 90 stores in El Salvador (under the Despensa Familiar (60 locations), La Despensa de Don Juan (17 locations), Walmart Supercenter (4 locations), and Maxi Despensa (9 locations) banners),<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 95 stores in Honduras (including the Paiz (8 locations), Walmart Supercenter (3 locations), Dispensa Familiar (64 locations), and Maxi Despensa (20 locations) banners),<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 92 stores in Nicaragua (including the Pali (65 locations), La Unión (8 locations), Maxi Pali (18 locations), and Walmart Supercenter (1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>location) banners),<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> and 234 stores in Costa Rica (including the Maxi Pali (38 locations), Mas X Menos (34 locations), Walmart Supercenter (9<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations), and Pali (153 locations) banners<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-sec2006_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sec2006-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Chile">Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Chile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In January 2009, the company acquired a controlling interest in the largest grocer in <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, Distribución y Servicio D&amp;S SA.<sup id="cite_ref-Stanford_13_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stanford_13-115">[115]</a></sup> and<sup id="cite_ref-Bustillo_08_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bustillo_08-116">[116]</a></sup> In 2010, the company was renamed <a href="/wiki/Walmart_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Walmart Chile">Walmart Chile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Diario_Financiero_10_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diario_Financiero_10-117">[117]</a></sup> As of January 31, 2017, Walmart Chile operates 363 stores under the banners Lider (83 locations), Lider Express (82 locations), Superbodega Acuenta (106 locations), Ekono (88 locations), and Central Mayorista (4 locations).<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Walmart_de_M%C3%A9xico_y_Centroam%C3%A9rica" title="Walmart de México y Centroamérica">Walmart de México y Centroamérica</a></div>
<p>Walmart's Mexico division, the largest outside the U.S., as of January 31, 2017, consists of 2,411 stores.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> Walmart in Mexico operates Walmart Supercenter (262 locations), Sam's Club (160 locations), Bodega Aurrera (488 locations), Mi Bodega Aurrera (331 locations), Bodega Aurrera Express (942 locations), Superama (96 locations), Suburbia (117 locations), Medimart Farmacia de Walmart (10 locations), and Zona Suburbia (5<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations).<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada_and_EMEA">Canada and EMEA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Canada and EMEA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As of January 31, 2016, there are a total of 1,453 stores in Canada and <a href="/wiki/Europe,_the_Middle_East_and_Africa" title="Europe, the Middle East and Africa">Europe, the Middle East and Africa</a> (EMEA), which the latter consists of locations in the United Kingdom, South Africa, Botswana, Ghana, Kenya, Lesotho, Malawi, Mozambique, Namibia, Nigeria, Swaziland, Tanzania, Uganda, and Zambia.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Walmart_Canada" title="Walmart Canada">Walmart Canada</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WalmartRichmondHill.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/WalmartRichmondHill.JPG/220px-WalmartRichmondHill.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/WalmartRichmondHill.JPG/330px-WalmartRichmondHill.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/WalmartRichmondHill.JPG/440px-WalmartRichmondHill.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WalmartRichmondHill.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Walmart Supercentre in <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Hill,_Ontario" title="Richmond Hill, Ontario">Richmond Hill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Walmart has operated in Canada since it acquired 122<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>stores comprising the <a href="/wiki/Woolco" title="Woolco">Woolco</a> division of <a href="/wiki/F._W._Woolworth_Company" title="F. W. Woolworth Company">Woolworth Canada, Inc</a> in 1994. As of January 31, 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it operates 410<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations (including 330<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>supercentres and 80 discount stores)<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> and, as of June 2015, it employs 89,358 people, with a local home office in <a href="/wiki/Mississauga" title="Mississauga">Mississauga</a>, Ontario.<sup id="cite_ref-WalmartCanada_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WalmartCanada-118">[118]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Walmart_Canada" title="Walmart Canada">Walmart Canada</a>'s first three Supercentres (spelled as in <a href="/wiki/Canadian_English" title="Canadian English">Canadian English</a>) opened in November 2006 in <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Hamilton, Ontario">Hamilton</a>, <a href="/wiki/London,_Ontario" title="London, Ontario">London</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aurora,_Ontario" title="Aurora, Ontario">Aurora</a>, Ontario. The 100th<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Canadian Supercentre opened in July 2010, in <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria, British Columbia">Victoria, British Columbia</a>.</p>
<p>In 2010, Walmart Canada Bank was introduced with the launch of the Walmart Rewards MasterCard.<sup id="cite_ref-walmart_canada_bank_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walmart_canada_bank-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_big_green_sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_781233.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/A_big_green_sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_781233.jpg/220px-A_big_green_sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_781233.jpg" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/A_big_green_sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_781233.jpg/330px-A_big_green_sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_781233.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/A_big_green_sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_781233.jpg/440px-A_big_green_sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_781233.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="543" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_big_green_sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_781233.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Walmart's UK subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Walmart's UK subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a> (which retained its name after being acquired by Walmart) accounted for 42.7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent of 2006 sales of Walmart's international division. In contrast to the U.S. operations, Asda was originally and still remains primarily a grocery chain, but with a stronger focus on non-food items than most UK supermarket chains other than <a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">Tesco</a>. As of January 31, 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Asda had 631 stores,<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> including 147 from the 2010 acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Netto_UK" title="Netto UK">Netto UK</a>. In addition to small suburban Asda Supermarkets, which has 206 locations,<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> larger stores are branded Supercentres, which has 32 locations.<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> Other banners include Asda Superstores (339 locations), Asda Living (33 locations), and Asda Petrol Fueling Station (21 locations).<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> In July 2015, Asda updated its logo featuring the Walmart Asterisks behind the first 'A' in the Logo.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>On September 28, 2010, Walmart announced it would buy <a href="/wiki/Massmart_Holdings_Ltd" class="mw-redirect" title="Massmart Holdings Ltd">Massmart Holdings Ltd</a>. of <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> in a deal worth over <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$4<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span> giving the company its first footprint in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-Wake_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wake-121">[121]</a></sup> As of January 31, 2017, it has 373<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>stores in South Africa (under the banners Game Foodco (69 locations), CBW (47 locations), Game (50 locations), Builders Express (43 locations), Builders Warehouse (33 locations), Cambridge (37 locations), Dion Wired (24 locations), Rhino (20 locations), Makro (20 locations), Builders Trade Depot (15 locations), Jumbo (7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations), and Builders Superstore (8<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations)),<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 11 stores in Botswana (under the banners CBW (7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations), Game Foodco (2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations), and Builders Warehouse (2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations)),<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>store in Ghana (under the Game banner),<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>store in Kenya (under the Game Foodco banner),<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 3<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>stores in Lesotho (under the banners CBW (2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations) and Game (1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>location)),<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup> 2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>stores in Malawi (under the Game banner),<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 5<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>stores in Mozambique (under the banners Builders Warehouse (2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations), Game Foodco (2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations), and CBW (1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>location)),<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 4<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>stores in Namibia (under the banners Game Foodco (2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations), Game (1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>location), and CBW (1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>location)),<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 5<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>stores in Nigeria (under the banners Game (4<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations) and Game Foodco (1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>location),<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 1 store in Swaziland (under the CBW banner),<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-31" class="reference"><a id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>store in Uganda (under the Game banner),<sup Warehouse (1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>location)).<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20170212_Bilingual_signs_in_Walmart_Hangzhou_Toys.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/20170212_Bilingual_signs_in_Walmart_Hangzhou_Toys.jpg/220px-20170212_Bilingual_signs_in_Walmart_Hangzhou_Toys.jpg" width="220" height="297" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/20170212_Bilingual_signs_in_Walmart_Hangzhou_Toys.jpg/330px-20170212_Bilingual_signs_in_Walmart_Hangzhou_Toys.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/20170212_Bilingual_signs_in_Walmart_Hangzhou_Toys.jpg/440px-20170212_Bilingual_signs_in_Walmart_Hangzhou_Toys.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2976" data-file-height="4020" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20170212_Bilingual_signs_in_Walmart_Hangzhou_Toys.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Walmart in <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a>, China</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of January 31, 2017, there are currently a total of 800 stores in three Asian countries: China, Japan, and India.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Walmart has joint ventures in China and several majority-owned subsidiaries. As of January 31, 2017, Walmart China (沃尔玛 <i>Wò'ērmǎ</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> operates 439 stores under the Walmart Supercenter (402 locations), Sam's Club (15 locations), Neighborhood Market (2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations), Smart Choice (1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>location), and Hypermarket (19 locations) banners.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> In Japan, Walmart owns 100 percent of <a href="/wiki/Seiyu_Group" title="Seiyu Group">Seiyu</a> (西友 <i>Seiyū</i>) as of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Boyle_09_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boyle_09-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> As of January 31, 2017, there are 341 stores under the Seiyu (Hypermarket) (94 locations), Seiyu (Supermarket) (237 locations), Seiyu (General Merchandise) (1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>location), and Livin (9<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>locations) banners.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2012, Walmart announced that the company raises its stake to 51 percent in Chinese online supermarket <a href="/wiki/Yihaodian" title="Yihaodian">Yihaodian</a> to tap rising consumer wealth and help the company offer more products. Walmart took full ownership in July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Jourdan_15_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jourdan_15-125">[125]</a></sup> In November 2006, the company announced a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Bharti_Enterprises" title="Bharti Enterprises">Bharti Enterprises</a> to operate in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. As foreign corporations were not allowed to enter the retail sector directly, Walmart operated through franchises and handled the wholesale end of the business.<sup id="cite_ref-walmartindia_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walmartindia-126">[126]</a></sup> The partnership involves two joint ventures&#160;–&#160;Bharti manages the front end, involving opening of retail outlets while Walmart takes care of the back end, such as <a href="/wiki/Cold_chain" title="Cold chain">cold chains</a> and logistics. Walmart operates stores in India under the name Best Price Modern Wholesale.<sup id="cite_ref-Mathew_13_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mathew_13-127">[127]</a></sup> The first store opened in <a href="/wiki/Amritsar" title="Amritsar">Amritsar</a> on 30 May 2009. On September 14, 2012, the Government of India approved 51 percent FDI in multi-brand retails, subject to approval by individual states, effective September 20, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Scott Price, Walmart's president and CEO for Asia, told <a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a> that the company would be able to start opening Walmart stores in India within two years.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Expansion into India faced some significant problems. In November 2012, Walmart admitted to spending <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$25<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span> lobbying the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-indiatimes_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indiatimes-131">[131]</a></sup>‍—‌lobbying is conventionally considered bribery in India.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCnewsUS_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCnewsUS-132">[132]</a></sup> Walmart is conducting an internal investigation into potential violations of the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Corrupt_Practices_Act" title="Foreign Corrupt Practices Act">Foreign Corrupt Practices Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTinquiry_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTinquiry-133">[133]</a></sup> Bharti Walmart suspended a number of employees, rumored to include its CFO and legal team, to ensure "a complete and thorough investigation".<sup id="cite_ref-NYTIndianBribery_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTIndianBribery-134">[134]</a></sup> As of January 31, 2017, there are 20 Best Price locations.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> In October 2013, Bharti and Walmart separated to pursue businesses independently.<sup id="cite_ref-Times_of_India_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times_of_India-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Setbacks">Setbacks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Setbacks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the mid-1990s, Walmart tried with a large financial investment to get a foothold in the German retail market. In 1997, Walmart took over the supermarket chain Wertkauf with its 21 stores for DEM750<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> and in 1998, Walmart acquired 74 Interspar stores for DEM1.3<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>The German market at this point was an oligopoly with high competition among companies which used a similar low price strategy as Walmart. As a result, Walmart's low price strategy yielded no competitive advantage. Also, Walmart's <a href="/wiki/Organizational_culture" title="Organizational culture">corporate culture</a> was not viewed positively among employees and customers, particularly Walmart's "statement of ethics", which restricted relationships between employees and led to a public discussion in the media, resulting in a bad reputation among customers.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2006, Walmart announced its withdrawal from Germany due to sustained losses. The stores were sold to the German company <a href="/wiki/Metro_AG" title="Metro AG">Metro</a> during Walmart's fiscal third quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-Boyle_09_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boyle_09-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-walmartgermany_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walmartgermany-141">[141]</a></sup> Walmart did not disclose its losses from its German investment, but they were estimated to be around €3&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption_charges">Corruption charges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Corruption charges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>An April 2012 investigative report by <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported the allegations of a former executive of Walmart de Mexico that, in September 2005, the company had paid <a href="/wiki/Bribery" title="Bribery">bribes</a> via local fixers to officials throughout Mexico in exchange for construction permits, information, and other favors, which gave Walmart a substantial advantage over competitors.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTBribe_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTBribe-143">[143]</a></sup> Walmart investigators found credible evidence that Mexican and American laws had been broken. Concerns were also raised that Walmart executives in the United States had "hushed up" the allegations. A follow-up investigation by <i>The New York Times,</i> published December 17, 2012, revealed evidence that regulatory permission for siting, construction, and operation of nineteen stores had been obtained through bribery. There was evidence that a bribe of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$52,000</span> was paid to change a zoning map, which enabled the opening of a Walmart store a mile from a historical site in <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Teotihuac%C3%A1n" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan Teotihuacán">San Juan Teotihuacán</a> in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT92904_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT92904-144">[144]</a></sup> After the initial article was released, Walmart released a statement denying the allegations and describing its anti-corruption policy. While an official Walmart report states that it had found no evidence of corruption, the article alleges that previous internal reports had indeed turned up such evidence before the story became public.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> contributor Adam Hartung also commented that the bribery scandal was a reflection of Walmart's "serious management and strategy troubles", stating, "[s]candals are now commonplace<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... [e]ach scandal points out that Walmart's strategy is harder to navigate and is running into big problems".<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of December 2012, internal investigations were ongoing into possible violations of the Foreign Corrupt Practices Act.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT121712_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT121712-147">[147]</a></sup> Walmart has invested <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$99<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span> on internal investigations, which expanded beyond Mexico to implicate operations in China, Brazil, and India.<sup id="cite_ref-Clifford_12_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clifford_12-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brown_12_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown_12-149">[149]</a></sup> The case has added fuel to the debate as to whether foreign investment will result in increased prosperity, or if it merely allows local retail trade and economic policy to be taken over by "foreign financial and corporate interests".<sup id="cite_ref-Sharma_12_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sharma_12-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTIndia_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTIndia-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sam.27s_Club">Sam's Club</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sam's Club">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Club" title="Sam's Club">Sam's Club</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sam%27s_Club_store.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Sam%27s_Club_store.jpg/220px-Sam%27s_Club_store.jpg" width="220" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Sam%27s_Club_store.jpg/330px-Sam%27s_Club_store.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Sam%27s_Club_store.jpg/440px-Sam%27s_Club_store.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2364" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sam%27s_Club_store.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Sam's Club store in <a href="/wiki/Maplewood,_Missouri" title="Maplewood, Missouri">Maplewood, Missouri</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Sam's Club</b> is a chain of <a href="/wiki/Warehouse_club" title="Warehouse club">warehouse clubs</a> that sell groceries and <a href="/wiki/General_merchandise" class="mw-redirect" title="General merchandise">general merchandise</a>, often in bulk. They range from 71,000 to 168,000 square feet (6,600 to 15,600 square meters), with an average size of 134,000 square feet (12,400 square meters). Sam's Clubs are membership warehouse clubs where most customers buy annual memberships. There are three kinds of memberships of Sam's Club: Sam's Plus, Sam's Business and Sam's Savings. Each of these memberships provides customers various benefits and convenience.<sup id="cite_ref-Sams_Club_Membership_Benefits_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sams_Club_Membership_Benefits-152">[152]</a></sup> However, non-members can make purchases either by buying a one-day membership or paying a surcharge based on the price of the purchase.<sup id="cite_ref-aboutsamsclub_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutsamsclub-153">[153]</a></sup> Some locations also sell gasoline.<sup id="cite_ref-CSNews_WMGas_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSNews_WMGas-90">[90]</a></sup> The first Sam's Club opened in 1983 in <a href="/wiki/Midwest_City,_Oklahoma" title="Midwest City, Oklahoma">Midwest City, Oklahoma</a><sup id="cite_ref-aboutsamsclub_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutsamsclub-153">[153]</a></sup> under the name "Sam's Wholesale Club".</p>
<p>Sam's Club has found a niche market in recent years as a supplier to small businesses. All Sam's Clubs are open early hours exclusively for business members and their old slogan was "We're in Business for Small Business." Their slogan has been "Savings Made Simple" since late 2009, as Sam's Club attempts to attract a more diverse member base.<sup id="cite_ref-aboutsamsclub_153-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutsamsclub-153">[153]</a></sup> In March 2009, the company announced that it plans to enter the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_medical_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronic medical record">electronic medical records</a> business by offering a software package to physicians in small practices for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$25,000</span>. Walmart is partnering with <a href="/wiki/Dell" title="Dell">Dell</a> and eClinicalWorks.com in this new venture.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sam's Club's sales were <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$56.828<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span>, or 11.9<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent of total Walmart sales, during fiscal 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-2016_Annual_Report_Page_20_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_Annual_Report_Page_20-14">[14]</a></sup> As of January 31, 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 660<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Sam's Clubs in 47 states and Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> Oregon, Rhode Island (which that state's only location closed in 2016), Vermont, and the District of Columbia are the only states and territories where a Sam's Club does not operate. Walmart, through Walmart International, also operates 202<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>international Sam's Clubs, including 160<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>in Mexico,<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup> 27<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup> and 15<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>in China.<sup id="cite_ref-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage_1-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Information_for_Walmart_Investors:_Unit_Counts_.26_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_eCommerce">Global eCommerce</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Global eCommerce">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Based in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, California, Walmart's Global eCommerce division provides online retailing for Walmart, Sam's Club, ASDA, and all other international brands. There are several locations in the United States located in California and Oregon. They are <a href="/wiki/San_Bruno,_California" title="San Bruno, California">San Bruno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunnyvale,_California" title="Sunnyvale, California">Sunnyvale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brisbane,_California" title="Brisbane, California">Brisbane</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland</a>. Locations outside of the United States include <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> (<a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>), <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> (<a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a> (<a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsidiaries">Subsidiaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Subsidiaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vudu">Vudu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Vudu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vudu_2014_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Vudu_2014_logo.svg/220px-Vudu_2014_logo.svg.png" width="220" height="61" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Vudu_2014_logo.svg/330px-Vudu_2014_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Vudu_2014_logo.svg/440px-Vudu_2014_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="83" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vudu_2014_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Vudu logo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In February 2010, Walmart agreed to buy <a href="/wiki/Vudu" title="Vudu">Vudu</a>, a Silicon Valley start-up whose online movie service is being built into an increasing number of televisions and Blu-ray players. Terms of the acquisition were not disclosed, but a person briefed on the deal said the price for the company, which raised <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$60<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span> in capital, was over <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$100<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Stone_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stone-155">[155]</a></sup> It is the third most popular online movie service, with a market share of 5.3 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Private_label_brands">Private label brands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Private label brands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Walmart_brands" title="List of Walmart brands">List of Walmart brands</a></div>
<p>About 40 percent of products sold in Walmart are <a href="/wiki/Private_label" title="Private label">private label</a> <a href="/wiki/Store_brand" title="Store brand">store brands</a>, which are produced for the company through contracts with manufacturers. Walmart began offering private label brands in 1991, with the launch of <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Choice" title="Sam's Choice">Sam's Choice</a>, a line of drinks produced by <a href="/wiki/Cott" title="Cott">Cott</a> Beverages for Walmart. Sam's Choice quickly became popular and by 1993, was the third most popular beverage brand in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-samschoice_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-samschoice-157">[157]</a></sup> Other Walmart brands include Great Value and Equate in the U.S. and Canada and <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Smart Price</a> in Britain. A 2006 study talked of "the magnitude of mind-share Walmart appears to hold in the shoppers' minds when it comes to the awareness of private label brands and retailers."<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment">Entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2010, the company teamed with <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a> to produce <i><a href="/wiki/Secrets_of_the_Mountain" title="Secrets of the Mountain">Secrets of the Mountain</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jensen_Project" title="The Jensen Project">The Jensen Project</a></i>, two-hour family movies which featured the characters using Walmart and Procter &amp; Gamble branded products. <i>The Jensen Project</i> also featured a preview of a product to be released in several months in Walmart stores.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-la_times_review_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-la_times_review-160">[160]</a></sup> A third movie, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Walk_in_My_Shoes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="A Walk in My Shoes (page does not exist)">A Walk in My Shoes</a></i>, also aired in 2010 and a fourth is in production.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (November 2012)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Walmart's director of brand marketing also serves as co-chair of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_National_Advertisers" title="Association of National Advertisers">Association of National Advertisers</a>'s Alliance for Family Entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Moosejaw">Moosejaw</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Moosejaw">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On February 15, 2017, Walmart acquired <a href="/wiki/Moosejaw" title="Moosejaw">Moosejaw</a>, an online active outdoor retailer, for approximately $51 million. Moosejaw brought with it more than 400 brands, including <a href="/wiki/Patagonia_(clothing)" title="Patagonia (clothing)">Patagonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_North_Face" title="The North Face">The North Face</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marmot_(company)" title="Marmot (company)">Marmot</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arc%E2%80%99teryx" class="mw-redirect" title="Arc’teryx">Arc’teryx</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Home_Office_sign.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Walmart_Home_Office_sign.jpg/220px-Walmart_Home_Office_sign.jpg" width="220" height="308" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Walmart_Home_Office_sign.jpg/330px-Walmart_Home_Office_sign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Walmart_Home_Office_sign.jpg/440px-Walmart_Home_Office_sign.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="2100" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Home_Office_sign.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Home Office in <a href="/wiki/Bentonville,_Arkansas" title="Bentonville, Arkansas">Bentonville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Walmart is headquartered in the Walmart Home Office complex in <a href="/wiki/Bentonville,_Arkansas" title="Bentonville, Arkansas">Bentonville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>. The company's <a href="/wiki/Business_model" title="Business model">business model</a> is based on selling a wide variety of general merchandise at low prices.<sup id="cite_ref-2015_Annual_Report_Page_19_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015_Annual_Report_Page_19-10">[10]</a></sup> Doug McMillon became Walmart's CEO on February 1, 2014. McMillon began his Walmart career in warehouses while in high school. He has also worked as the head of Sam's Club and Walmart International.<sup id="cite_ref-O.27Keefe_15_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Keefe_15-164">[164]</a></sup> The company refers to employees as "associates". All Walmart stores in the U.S. and Canada also have designated "greeters" at the entrance, a practice pioneered by <a href="/wiki/Sam_Walton" title="Sam Walton">Sam Walton</a> and later imitated by other retailers. Greeters are trained to help shoppers find what they want and answer their questions.<sup id="cite_ref-Kendall_Gerald_I_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kendall_Gerald_I-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>For many years, associates were identified in the store by their signature blue vest, but this practice was discontinued in June 2007 and replaced with khaki pants and polo shirts. The wardrobe change was part of a larger corporate overhaul to increase sales and rejuvenate the company's stock price.<sup id="cite_ref-replace_blue_vests_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-replace_blue_vests-166">[166]</a></sup> In September 2014, the uniform was again updated to bring back a vest (paid for by the company) for store employees over the same polo's and khaki or black pants paid for by the employee. The vest is navy blue for Walmart employees at Supercenters and discount stores and lime green for Walmart Neighborhood Market employees, both state "Proud Walmart Associate" on the left breast and the "Spark" logo covering the back.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Reportedly one of the main reasons the vest was reintroduced was because some customers had trouble identifying employees.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> By requiring employees to wear uniforms that are made up of standard "street wear", Walmart is not required to purchase or reimbursement employees which is required in some states, as long as that clothing can be worn elsewhere. Businesses are only legally required to pay for branded shirts and pants or clothes that would be difficult to wear outside of work.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p>
<p>Unlike many other retailers, Walmart does not charge <a href="/wiki/Slotting_fee" title="Slotting fee">slotting fees</a> to suppliers for their products to appear in the store.<sup id="cite_ref-nelson_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nelson-170">[170]</a></sup> Instead, it focuses on selling more popular products and provides incentives for store managers to drop unpopular products.<sup id="cite_ref-nelson_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nelson-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 14, 2006, the company announced that it would phase out its <a href="/wiki/Layaway" title="Layaway">layaway</a> program, citing declining use and increased costs.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Layaway ceased on November 19, 2006, and required merchandise pickup by December 8, 2006. Walmart now focuses on other payment options, such as increased use of six- and twelve-month, zero-interest financing. The layaway location in most stores is now used for Walmart's Site-To-Store program, which was introduced in March 2007. This enables <i>walmart.com</i> customers to buy goods online with a free shipping option, and have goods shipped to the nearest store for pickup.<sup id="cite_ref-site-to-store_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-site-to-store-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance_and_governance">Finance and governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Finance and governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For the <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year" title="Fiscal year">fiscal year</a> ending January 31, 2015, Walmart reported <a href="/wiki/Net_income" title="Net income">net income</a> of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$17<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span> on <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$485.7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span> of revenue. The company's international operations accounted for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$197.7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span>, or 40.7 percent, of sales.<sup id="cite_ref-Form10K_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Form10K-5">[5]</a></sup> Walmart is the world's 18th largest public corporation, according to the <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Global_2000" title="Forbes Global 2000">Forbes Global 2000</a> list, and the largest public corporation when ranked by revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes_global_2000_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes_global_2000-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p>Walmart is governed by a fifteen-member Board of Directors elected annually by <a href="/wiki/Shareholder" title="Shareholder">shareholders</a>. <a href="/wiki/Gregory_B._Penner" class="mw-redirect" title="Gregory B. Penner">Gregory B. Penner</a>, son-in-law of <a href="/wiki/S._Robson_Walton" title="S. Robson Walton">S. Robson Walton</a> and the grandson-in-law of <a href="/wiki/Sam_Walton" title="Sam Walton">Sam Walton</a> serves as <a href="/wiki/Chairman" title="Chairman">Chairman</a> of the Board. <a href="/wiki/Doug_McMillon" title="Doug McMillon">Doug McMillon</a> serves as President and Chief Executive Officer. Members of the board include <a href="/wiki/A%C3%ADda_%C3%81lvarez" title="Aída Álvarez">Aída Álvarez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Breyer" title="Jim Breyer">Jim Breyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/M._Michele_Burns" title="M. Michele Burns">M. Michele Burns</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Cash,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="James Cash, Jr.">James Cash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Corbett" title="Roger Corbett">Roger Corbett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Daft" title="Douglas Daft">Douglas Daft</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Glass_(businessman)" title="David Glass (businessman)">David Glass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marissa_Mayer" title="Marissa Mayer">Marissa Mayer</a>, Allen Questrom, Arne M. Sorenson, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Walton" title="Jim Walton">Jim Walton</a>, <a href="/wiki/S._Robson_Walton" title="S. Robson Walton">S. Robson Walton</a>, Christopher J. Williams, and Linda S. Wolf.<sup id="cite_ref-Form10K_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Form10K-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sorkin_Rusli_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sorkin_Rusli-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<p>Notable former members of the board include <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> (1985–1992)<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tom_Coughlin_(Walmart_executive)" title="Tom Coughlin (Walmart executive)">Tom Coughlin</a> (2003–2004), the latter having served as Vice Chairman. Clinton left the board before the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1992" title="United States presidential election, 1992">1992 U.S. Presidential Election</a>, and Coughlin left in December 2005 after pleading guilty to wire fraud and tax evasion for stealing hundreds of thousands of dollars from Walmart.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> On August 11, 2006, he was sentenced to 27 months home confinement, five years of probation, and ordered to pay <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$411,000</span> in restitution.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>After Sam Walton's death in 1992, Don Soderquist, Chief Operating Officer and Senior Vice Chairman, became known as the "Keeper of the Culture."<sup id="cite_ref-Soderquist_Donald_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soderquist_Donald-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>WAL-MART STORES, INC. is a <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company" title="Joint-stock company">joint-stock company</a> registered with the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">SEC</a>. As of March 2017<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> it has 3,292,377,090 outstanding shares. These are held mainly by the <a href="/wiki/Walton_family" title="Walton family">Walton family</a>, a number of <a href="/wiki/Institutional_investor" title="Institutional investor">institutions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mutual_fund" title="Mutual fund">funds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>43.00% (1,415,891,131): <a href="/wiki/Walton_family" title="Walton family">Walton Enterprises</a> LLC</li>
<li>5.30% (174,563,205): <a href="/wiki/Walton_family" title="Walton family">Walton Family</a> Holdings Trust<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></li>
<li>3.32% (102,036,399): <a href="/wiki/The_Vanguard_Group" title="The Vanguard Group">The Vanguard Group</a>, Inc</li>
<li>2.37% (72,714,226): <a href="/wiki/State_Street_Corporation" title="State Street Corporation">State Street Corporation</a></li>
<li>1.37% (42,171,892): <a href="/wiki/BlackRock" title="BlackRock">BlackRock</a> Institutional Trust Company</li>
<li>0.94% (28,831,721): <a href="/wiki/The_Vanguard_Group" title="The Vanguard Group">Vanguard</a> Total Stock Market Index Fund</li>
<li>0.77% (23,614,578): <a href="/wiki/BlackRock" title="BlackRock">BlackRock</a> Fund Advisors</li>
<li>0.71% (21,769,126): <a href="/wiki/Dodge_%26_Cox" title="Dodge &amp; Cox">Dodge &amp; Cox</a> Inc</li>
<li>0.68% (20,978,727): <a href="/wiki/The_Vanguard_Group" title="The Vanguard Group">Vanguard</a> 500 Index Fund</li>
<li>0.65% (20,125,838): <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a> Corporation</li>
<li>0.57% (17,571,058): <a href="/wiki/The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon" title="The Bank of New York Mellon">Bank of New York Mellon</a> Corporation</li>
<li>0.57% (17,556,128): <a href="/wiki/Northern_Trust" title="Northern Trust">Northern Trust</a> Corporation</li>
<li>0.55% (16,818,165): <a href="/wiki/The_Vanguard_Group" title="The Vanguard Group">Vanguard</a> Institutional Index Fund-Institutional Index Fund</li>
<li>0.55% (16,800,850): <a href="/wiki/State_Farm_Insurance" title="State Farm Insurance">State Farm</a> Mutual Automobile Insurance Co</li>
<li>0.52% (15,989,827): <a href="/wiki/SPDR" title="SPDR">SPDR</a> S&amp;P 500 ETF Trust</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition">Competition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Competition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In North America, Walmart's primary competitors include <a href="/wiki/Department_store" title="Department store">department stores</a> like <a href="/wiki/Aldi" title="Aldi">Aldi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kroger" title="Kroger">Kroger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ingles" title="Ingles">Ingles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Publix" title="Publix">Publix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shopko" title="Shopko">Shopko</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Meijer" title="Meijer">Meijer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Winn_Dixie" class="mw-redirect" title="Winn Dixie">Winn Dixie</a>, Canada's The <a href="/wiki/Real_Canadian_Superstore" title="Real Canadian Superstore">Real Canadian Superstore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giant_Tiger" title="Giant Tiger">Giant Tiger</a>, and Mexico's <a href="/wiki/Comercial_Mexicana" title="Comercial Mexicana">Comercial Mexicana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soriana" title="Soriana">Soriana</a>. Competitors of Walmart's Sam's Club division are <a href="/wiki/Costco" title="Costco">Costco</a> and the smaller <a href="/wiki/BJ%27s_Wholesale_Club" title="BJ's Wholesale Club">BJ's Wholesale Club</a> chain. Walmart's move into the grocery business in the late 1990s also set it against major supermarket chains in both the United States and Canada. Some retail analysts see regional grocery store chain <a href="/wiki/WinCo_Foods" title="WinCo Foods">WinCo Foods</a> as serious competition for Walmart.<sup id="cite_ref-TIME_winco_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TIME_winco-184">[184]</a></sup> Several smaller retailers, primarily <a href="/wiki/Variety_store" title="Variety store">dollar stores</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Family_Dollar" title="Family Dollar">Family Dollar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dollar_General" title="Dollar General">Dollar General</a>, have been able to find a small niche market and compete successfully against Walmart.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> In 2004, Walmart responded by testing its own dollar store concept, a subsection of some stores called "Pennies-n-Cents."<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<p>Walmart also had to face fierce competition in some foreign markets. For example, in Germany it had captured just 2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent of the German food market following its entry into the market in 1997 and remained "a secondary player" behind <a href="/wiki/Aldi" title="Aldi">Aldi</a> with 19<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent.<sup id="cite_ref-Struggling_In_Germany_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Struggling_In_Germany-187">[187]</a></sup> Walmart continues to do well in the UK, where its <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a> subsidiary is the second largest retailer.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Bumpy_Ride_in_Europe_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Bumpy_Ride_in_Europe-188">[188]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2006, after entering the South Korean market in 1998, Walmart sold all 16<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>of its South Korean outlets to <a href="/wiki/Shinsegae" title="Shinsegae">Shinsegae</a>, a local retailer, for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$882<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million</span>. Shinsegae re-branded the Walmarts as <a href="/wiki/E-mart" title="E-mart">E-mart</a> stores.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_wmt_skorea_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_wmt_skorea-189">[189]</a></sup></p>
<p>Walmart struggled to export its brand elsewhere as it rigidly tried to reproduce its model overseas. In China, Walmart hopes to succeed by adapting and doing things preferable to Chinese citizens. For example, it found that Chinese consumers preferred to select their own live fish and seafood; stores began displaying the meat uncovered and installed fish tanks, leading to higher sales.<sup id="cite_ref-China_reinvent_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China_reinvent-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Customer_base">Customer base</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Customer base">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:15-cent_prices_on_notebooks_at_Walmart.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/15-cent_prices_on_notebooks_at_Walmart.jpg/220px-15-cent_prices_on_notebooks_at_Walmart.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/15-cent_prices_on_notebooks_at_Walmart.jpg/330px-15-cent_prices_on_notebooks_at_Walmart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/15-cent_prices_on_notebooks_at_Walmart.jpg/440px-15-cent_prices_on_notebooks_at_Walmart.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:15-cent_prices_on_notebooks_at_Walmart.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A price of 15 cents on folders and notebooks</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Walmart customers cite low prices as the most important reason for shopping there.<sup id="cite_ref-nytmorethanprice_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytmorethanprice-191">[191]</a></sup> The average U.S. Walmart customer's income is below the national average, and analysts estimated that more than one-fifth of them lack a bank account; twice the national rate.<sup id="cite_ref-walmart2006_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walmart2006-192">[192]</a></sup> A 2006 Walmart report also indicated that Walmart customers are sensitive to higher utility costs and gas prices.<sup id="cite_ref-walmart2006_192-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walmart2006-192">[192]</a></sup> A poll indicated that after the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2004" title="United States presidential election, 2004">2004 US Presidential Election</a>, 76<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent of voters who shopped at Walmart once a week voted for <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> while only 23 percent supported senator <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-zogbypoll_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zogbypoll-193">[193]</a></sup> When measured against similar retailers in the U.S., frequent Walmart shoppers were rated the most politically <a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Conservatism in the United States">conservative</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> Thus, as of 2014, the "majority (54<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>percent) [of] Americans who prefer shopping at Walmart report that they oppose <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a>, while 40 percent are in favor of it."<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due to its prominence in the <a href="/wiki/Bible_Belt" title="Bible Belt">Bible Belt</a>, Walmart is known for its "tradition of tailoring its service to churchgoing customers".<sup id="cite_ref-Gilgoff_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gilgoff-196">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sellers_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sellers-197">[197]</a></sup> Walmart only carries <a href="/w/index.php?title=Censorship_of_music&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Censorship of music (page does not exist)">clean versions</a> of hip-hop <a href="/wiki/Compact_Disc" class="mw-redirect" title="Compact Disc">audio CDs</a> and in cooperation with <a href="/wiki/The_Timothy_Plan" title="The Timothy Plan">The Timothy Plan</a>, places "plastic sheathes over suggestive women's periodicals and banned 'lad mags' such as <a href="/wiki/Maxim_(magazine)" title="Maxim (magazine)">Maxim</a>" magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-Gilgoff_196-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gilgoff-196">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sellers_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sellers-197">[197]</a></sup> In addition, Walmart also caters to its Christian customer base by selling <a href="/wiki/Christian_media" title="Christian media">Christian books and media</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Gilgoff_196-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gilgoff-196">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Collidge_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collidge-198">[198]</a></sup> "such as <a href="/wiki/VeggieTales" title="VeggieTales">VeggieTales</a> videos and <a href="/wiki/The_Purpose-Driven_Life" class="mw-redirect" title="The Purpose-Driven Life">The Purpose-Driven Life</a>", which earns the company over <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion</span> annually.<sup id="cite_ref-Collidge_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collidge-198">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sellers2_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sellers2-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, Walmart took steps to expand its U.S. customer base, announcing a modification in its U.S. stores from a "one-size-fits-all" merchandising strategy to one designed to "reflect each of six demographic groups&#160;–&#160;African-Americans, the affluent, empty-nesters, Hispanics, suburbanites, and rural residents."<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_06_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_06-200">[200]</a></sup> Around six months later, it unveiled a new slogan: <i>"Saving people money so they can live better lives"</i>. This reflects the three main groups into which Walmart categorizes its 200<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million customers: "brand aspirationals" (people with low incomes who are obsessed with names like <a href="/wiki/KitchenAid" title="KitchenAid">KitchenAid</a>), "price-sensitive affluents" (wealthier shoppers who love deals), and "value-price shoppers" (people who like low prices and cannot afford much more).<sup id="cite_ref-nytmorethanprice_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytmorethanprice-191">[191]</a></sup> Walmart has also made steps to appeal to more <a href="/wiki/Liberalism_in_the_United_States" title="Liberalism in the United States">liberal</a> customers, for example, by rejecting the <a href="/wiki/American_Family_Association" title="American Family Association">American Family Association</a>'s recommendations and carrying the DVD <i><a href="/wiki/Brokeback_Mountain" title="Brokeback Mountain">Brokeback Mountain</a>,</i> a love story between two gay cowboys in Wyoming.<sup id="cite_ref-brokeback_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brokeback-201">[201]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_Source_Software">Open Source Software</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Open Source Software">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
